I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
bug: [GC] WasmEdge crash: `ref.test`/`ref.cast` on default-initialized local with concrete ref type
### Summary

# WasmEdge SIGSEGV: `ref.test`/`ref.cast` on default-initialized local with concrete ref type

## Version

- WasmEdge `77c5238980b3c9cd8fc7e7dc69b20127d9fd68ca` (includes fix from #4764)
- Linux 5.15.0-168-generic x86\_64

## Relation to #4757 / #4764

This is the **same crash site** as #4757 (`runRefTestOp` null-pointer dereference in `refInstr.cpp:339`), but a **different source** of the concrete-typed null. PR #4764 fixed the table-initialization path; this bug is in the **function-local initialization** path and remains unfixed on current `master`.

## Minimal Reproducer

```wat
(module
  (type $s (struct))
  (func (export "run")
    (local (ref null $s))
    local.get 0
    ref.test (ref null $s)
    drop
  )
)
```

```bash
wasm-tools parse crash.wat -o crash.wasm
wasm-tools validate crash.wasm   # OK
wasmedge crash.wasm run          # Segmentation fault
wasmtime run --wasm gc --invoke run crash.wasm  # OK
```

## (Potential) Root Cause

`ValueFromType` ([include/common/types.h:680](https://github.com/WasmEdge/WasmEdge/blob/77c5238980b3c9cd8fc7e7dc69b20127d9fd68ca/include/common/types.h#L680)) initializes reference-typed locals with `RefVariant(Type)`, passing the **raw concrete type** (e.g. `(ref null $s)`). This creates a null `RefVariant` whose `ValType` has `HTCode = TypeIndex`, violating the invariant that null references always carry abstract heap types.

When `ref.test` or `ref.cast` later calls `runRefTestOp` ([lib/executor/engine/refInstr.cpp:334-339](https://github.com/WasmEdge/WasmEdge/blob/77c5238980b3c9cd8fc7e7dc69b20127d9fd68ca/lib/executor/engine/refInstr.cpp#L334-L339)):

```cpp
if (!VT.isAbsHeapType()) {                       // true — TypeIndex is not abstract
    auto *Inst = Val.get<RefVariant>()
                    .getPtr<Runtime::Instance::CompositeBase>();
    // "Reference must not be nullptr here because the null references
    //  are typed with the least abstract heap type."
    if (Inst->getModule()) {                      // CRASH — Inst is nullptr
```

This is the same invariant violation fixed for tables in #4764, but through a different entry point.

Either normalize the type in `ValueFromType` (requires access to the module to call `toBottomType`), or normalize in `enterFunction` ([lib/executor/helper.cpp:212-216](https://github.com/WasmEdge/WasmEdge/blob/77c5238980b3c9cd8fc7e7dc69b20127d9fd68ca/lib/executor/helper.cpp#L212-L216)) where locals are pushed onto the stack — mirroring the approach used for tables in #4764.

## Acknowledgement

This bug was found during the development of GCsmith.

   441	// The bit pattern of the component value types:
   442	// ----------------------------------------------------
   443	//  byte |      0th ~ 3rd       |      4th ~ 7th
   444	// ------|----------------------|----------------------
   445	//  code | ComponentValTypeCode |      Type index
   446	// ----------------------------------------------------
   447	
   448	/// ComponentValType class definition.
   449	class ComponentValType {
   450	public:
   451	  // Note: The padding bytes are reserved and should not be written.
   452	  ComponentValType() noexcept = default;
   453	  // General constructors for initializing data.
   454	  ComponentValType(ComponentTypeCode C, uint32_t I) noexcept {
   455	    Inner.Data.TCode = C;
   456	    Inner.Data.Idx = I;
   457	  }
   458	  ComponentValType(const std::array<uint8_t, 8> R) noexcept {
   459	    std::copy_n(R.cbegin(), 8, Inner.Raw);
   460	  }
   461	  // Constructor for the component value type with primvaltype.
   462	  ComponentValType(ComponentTypeCode C) noexcept {
   463	    Inner.Data.TCode = C;
   464	    Inner.Data.Idx = 0;
   465	    assuming(C != ComponentTypeCode::TypeIndex);
   466	  }
   467	  // Constructor for the component value type with type index.
   468	  ComponentValType(uint32_t I) noexcept {
   469	    Inner.Data.TCode = ComponentTypeCode::TypeIndex;
   470	    Inner.Data.Idx = I;
   471	  }
   472	
   473	  friend bool operator==(const ComponentValType &LHS,
   474	                         const ComponentValType &RHS) noexcept {
   475	    return (LHS.Inner.Data.TCode == RHS.Inner.Data.TCode) &&
   476	           (LHS.Inner.Data.Idx == RHS.Inner.Data.Idx);
   477	  }
   478	  friend bool operator!=(const ComponentValType &LHS,
   479	                         const ComponentValType &RHS) noexcept {
   480	    return !(LHS == RHS);
   481	  }
   482	
   483	  ComponentTypeCode getCode() const noexcept { return Inner.Data.TCode; }
   484	  uint32_t getTypeIndex() const noexcept { return Inner.Data.Idx; }
   485	  const std::array<uint8_t, 8> getRawData() const noexcept {
   486	    std::array<uint8_t, 8> R;
   487	    std::copy_n(Inner.Raw, 8, R.begin());
   488	    return R;
   489	  }
   490	
   491	  void setCode(const ComponentTypeCode C) noexcept {
   492	    Inner.Data.TCode = C;
   493	    Inner.Data.Idx = 0;
   494	  }
   495	  void setTypeIndex(const uint32_t I) noexcept {
   496	    Inner.Data.TCode = ComponentTypeCode::TypeIndex;
   497	    Inner.Data.Idx = I;
   498	  }
   499	  bool isPrimValType() const noexcept {
   500	    return Inner.Data.TCode != ComponentTypeCode::TypeIndex;
   501	  }
   502	
   503	private:
   504	  union {
   505	    uint8_t Raw[8];
   506	    struct {
   507	      uint8_t Padding[3];
   508	      ComponentTypeCode TCode;
   509	      uint32_t Idx;
   510	    } Data;
   511	  } Inner;
   512	};

   323	Expect<void>
   324	Executor::runRefTestOp(const Runtime::Instance::ModuleInstance *ModInst,
   325	                       ValVariant &Val, const AST::Instruction &Instr,
   326	                       const bool IsCast) const noexcept {
   327	  // Copy the value type here due to handling the externalized case.
   328	  auto VT = Val.get<RefVariant>().getType();
   329	  if (VT.isExternalized()) {
   330	    VT = ValType(VT.isNullableRefType() ? TypeCode::RefNull : TypeCode::Ref,
   331	                 TypeCode::ExternRef);
   332	  }
   333	  Span<const AST::SubType *const> GotTypeList = ModInst->getTypeList();
   334	  if (!VT.isAbsHeapType()) {
   335	    auto *Inst =
   336	        Val.get<RefVariant>().getPtr<Runtime::Instance::CompositeBase>();
   337	    // Reference must not be nullptr here because the null references are typed
   338	    // with the least abstract heap type.
   339	    if (Inst->getModule()) {
   340	      GotTypeList = Inst->getModule()->getTypeList();
   341	    }
   342	  }
   343	
   344	  if (AST::TypeMatcher::matchType(ModInst->getTypeList(), Instr.getValType(),
   345	                                  GotTypeList, VT)) {
   346	    if (!IsCast) {
   347	      Val.emplace<uint32_t>(1U);
   348	    }
   349	  } else {
   350	    if (IsCast) {
   351	      spdlog::error(ErrCode::Value::CastFailed);
   352	      spdlog::error(ErrInfo::InfoMismatch(Instr.getValType(), VT));
   353	      spdlog::error(
   354	          ErrInfo::InfoInstruction(Instr.getOpCode(), Instr.getOffset()));
   355	      return Unexpect(ErrCode::Value::CastFailed);
   356	    } else {
   357	      Val.emplace<uint32_t>(0U);
   358	    }
   359	  }
   360	  return {};
   361	}
   362

   375	  } else {
   376	    // Externalize.
   377	    if (Ref.isNull()) {
   378	      Ref = RefVariant(ValType(TypeCode::RefNull, TypeCode::NullExternRef));
   379	    } else {
   380	      // Use the externalize flag because the value type information should be

   234	Expect<void>
   235	Executor::branchToLabel(Runtime::StackManager &StackMgr,
   236	                        const AST::Instruction::JumpDescriptor &JumpDesc,
   237	                        AST::InstrView::iterator &PC) noexcept {
   238	  // Check the stop token.
   239	  if (unlikely(StopToken.exchange(0, std::memory_order_relaxed))) {
   240	    spdlog::error(ErrCode::Value::Interrupted);
   241	    return Unexpect(ErrCode::Value::Interrupted);
   242	  }
   243	
   244	  StackMgr.eraseValueStack(JumpDesc.StackEraseBegin, JumpDesc.StackEraseEnd);
   245	  // PC need to -1 here because the PC will increase in the next iteration.
   246	  PC += (JumpDesc.PCOffset - 1);
   247	  return {};
   248	}

   420	}
   421	
   422	TypeCode Executor::toBottomType(Runtime::StackManager &StackMgr,
   423	                                const ValType &Type) const {
   424	  if (Type.isRefType()) {
   425	    if (Type.isAbsHeapType()) {
   426	      switch (Type.getHeapTypeCode()) {
   427	      case TypeCode::NullFuncRef:
   428	      case TypeCode::FuncRef:
   429	        return TypeCode::NullFuncRef;
   430	      case TypeCode::NullExternRef:
   431	      case TypeCode::ExternRef:
   432	        return TypeCode::NullExternRef;
   433	      case TypeCode::NullRef:
   434	      case TypeCode::AnyRef:
   435	      case TypeCode::EqRef:
   436	      case TypeCode::I31Ref:
   437	      case TypeCode::StructRef:
   438	      case TypeCode::ArrayRef:
   439	        return TypeCode::NullRef;
   440	      case TypeCode::NullExnRef:
   441	      case TypeCode::ExnRef:
   442	        return TypeCode::NullExnRef;
   443	      default:
   444	        assumingUnreachable();
   445	      }
   446	    } else {
   447	      const auto &CompType =
   448	          (*StackMgr.getModule()->getType(Type.getTypeIndex()))
   449	              ->getCompositeType();
   450	      if (CompType.isFunc()) {
   451	        return TypeCode::NullFuncRef;
   452	      } else {
   453	        return TypeCode::NullRef;
   454	      }
   455	    }
   456	  } else {
   457	    return Type.getCode();
   458	  }
   459	}
   460

     1	// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0
     2	// SPDX-FileCopyrightText: 2019-2024 Second State INC
     3	
     4	#include "executor/executor.h"
     5	
     6	#include <cstdint>
     7	
     8	namespace WasmEdge {
     9	namespace Executor {
    10	
    11	// Instantiate table instance. See "include/executor/executor.h".
    12	Expect<void> Executor::instantiate(Runtime::StackManager &StackMgr,
    13	                                   Runtime::Instance::ModuleInstance &ModInst,
    14	                                   const AST::TableSection &TabSec) {
    15	  // A frame with temp. module is pushed into the stack in caller.
    16	
    17	  // Iterate through the table segments to instantiate and initialize table
    18	  // instances.
    19	  for (const auto &TabSeg : TabSec.getContent()) {
    20	    if (TabSeg.getExpr().getInstrs().size() > 0) {
    21	      // Run initialize expression.
    22	      EXPECTED_TRY(runExpression(StackMgr, TabSeg.getExpr().getInstrs())
    23	                       .map_error([](auto E) {
    24	                         spdlog::error(
    25	                             ErrInfo::InfoAST(ASTNodeAttr::Expression));
    26	                         return E;
    27	                       }));
    28	      // Pop result from stack.
    29	      RefVariant InitTabValue = StackMgr.pop().get<RefVariant>();
    30	      // Create and add the table instance into the module instance.
    31	      ModInst.addTable(TabSeg.getTableType(), InitTabValue);
    32	    } else {
    33	      // No init expression case. Use the null reference to initialize.
    34	      // Normalize the type to the bottom abstract heap type so that null
    35	      // references always carry abstract types, as ref.cast/ref.test assume.
    36	      auto BotType = toBottomType(StackMgr, TabSeg.getTableType().getRefType());
    37	      RefVariant InitTabValue(ValType(TypeCode::RefNull, BotType));
    38	      ModInst.addTable(TabSeg.getTableType(), InitTabValue);
    39	    }
    40	  }
    41	  return {};
    42	}
    43	
    44	} // namespace Executor
    45	} // namespace WasmEdge

Now I understand the issue. Let's look at the `enterFunction` in `helper.cpp` more carefully. The problem is at line 214:

```cpp
StackMgr.push(ValueFromType(Def.second));
```

Where `ValueFromType` for a reference type (e.g., `(ref null $s)`) creates a `RefVariant(Type)` with the raw concrete type (with `HTCode = TypeIndex`). But when this is a null reference, it should instead have an abstract heap type (bottom type). The `ref.test`/`ref.cast` operations assume that null references always carry abstract heap types.

   666	inline ValVariant ValueFromType(ValType Type) noexcept {
   667	  switch (Type.getCode()) {
   668	  case TypeCode::I32:
   669	    return uint32_t(0U);
   670	  case TypeCode::I64:
   671	    return uint64_t(0U);
   672	  case TypeCode::F32:
   673	    return float(0.0F);
   674	  case TypeCode::F64:
   675	    return double(0.0);
   676	  case TypeCode::V128:
   677	    return uint128_t(0U);
   678	  case TypeCode::Ref:
   679	  case TypeCode::RefNull:
   680	    return RefVariant(Type);
   681	  default:
   682	    assumingUnreachable();
   683	  }

Now I see the problem. `ValueFromType` for reference types creates a `RefVariant(Type)` where `Type` could have a concrete type index (e.g., `(ref null $s)`). This creates a null `RefVariant` whose `ValType` has `HTCode = TypeIndex`. But the invariant that the code expects is that null references always carry abstract heap types.

The fix should be in `enterFunction` (helper.cpp) where locals are pushed onto the stack. We should normalize the type to the bottom abstract heap type for null references, similar to what was done for tables.

   550	/// Regression test for ref.cast on null refs from concrete-typed tables
   551	/// (issue #4757).
   552	///
   553	/// When ref.cast received a null reference with a concrete type, the code
   554	/// entered the `!VT.isAbsHeapType()` branch and dereferenced the null object
   555	/// pointer before checking for null, causing a segfault.
   556	///
   557	/// This test covers:
   558	///   - ref.cast eqref on null (nullable cast should pass through)
   559	///   - ref.cast (ref eq) on null (non-nullable cast should trap)
   560	TEST(ExecutorRegression, RefCastNullAbility) {
   561	  // --- Part 1: ref.cast eqref on null --- nullable cast passes through
   562	  {
   563	    Configure Conf;
   564	    VM::VM VM(Conf);
   565	    GCCheckModule GCMod;
   566	    VM.registerModule(GCMod);
   567	    ASSERT_TRUE(VM.loadWasm(NullRefCastWasm));
   568	    ASSERT_TRUE(VM.validate());
   569	    ASSERT_TRUE(VM.instantiate());
   570	    ASSERT_TRUE(checkNullTableEntry(VM));
   571	    VM.execute("test");
   572	    auto Values = GCMod.getValues();
   573	    ASSERT_EQ(Values.size(), 1);
   574	    EXPECT_EQ(Values[0], 1); // null passed through nullable cast
   575	  }
   576	
   577	  // --- Part 2: ref.cast (ref eq) on null --- non-nullable cast must trap
   578	  {
   579	    Configure Conf;
   580	    VM::VM VM(Conf);
   581	    GCCheckModule GCMod;
   582	    VM.registerModule(GCMod);
   583	    ASSERT_TRUE(VM.loadWasm(NullRefCastNonNullWasm));
   584	    ASSERT_TRUE(VM.validate());
   585	    ASSERT_TRUE(VM.instantiate());
   586	    ASSERT_TRUE(checkNullTableEntry(VM));
   587	    auto Result = VM.execute("test");
   588	    EXPECT_FALSE(Result); // should trap with CastFailed
   589	  }
   590	}

     1	// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0

     3	
     4	//===-- wasmedge/test/executor/ExecutorRegressionTest.cpp - Regression ----===//
     5	//
     6	// Part of the WasmEdge Project.
     7	//
     8	//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//
     9	///
    10	/// \file
    11	/// Regression and miscellaneous tests for the executor.
    12	///
    13	//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//
    14	
    15	#include "common/spdlog.h"
    16	#include "common/types.h"
    17	#include "vm/vm.h"
    18	
    19	#include <array>
    20	#include <cstdint>
    21	#include <gtest/gtest.h>
    22	#include <vector>
    23	
    24	namespace {
    25	
    26	using namespace WasmEdge;
    27	
    28	/// Host function that records i32 values for later inspection.
    29	class Check : public Runtime::HostFunction<Check> {
    30	public:
    31	  Expect<void> body(const Runtime::CallingFrame &, uint32_t Value) {
    32	    Values.push_back(Value);
    33	    return {};
    34	  }
    35	  Span<const uint32_t> getValues() const noexcept { return Values; }
    36	
    37	private:
    38	  std::vector<uint32_t> Values;
    39	};
    40	
    41	/// Module that provides a "check" host function under the "gc" namespace.
    42	class GCCheckModule : public Runtime::Instance::ModuleInstance {
    43	public:
    44	  GCCheckModule() : ModuleInstance("gc") {
    45	    auto CP = std::make_unique<Check>();
    46	    C = CP.get();
    47	    addHostFunc("check", std::move(CP));
    48	  }
    49	  Span<const uint32_t> getValues() const noexcept { return C->getValues(); }
    50	
    51	private:
    52	  Check *C = nullptr;
    53	};
    54	
    55	/// After instantiation, read the exported table "t" at index 0 and verify the
    56	/// null reference has been normalized to an abstract heap type. This catches
    57	/// the root cause of #4757 without executing wasm that would segfault if the
    58	/// fix is absent.
    59	bool checkNullTableEntry(VM::VM &VMInst) {
    60	  const auto *ModInst = VMInst.getActiveModule();
    61	  if (!ModInst) {
    62	    return false;
    63	  }
    64	  auto *TabInst = ModInst->findTableExports("t");
    65	  if (!TabInst) {
    66	    return false;
    67	  }
    68	  auto RefRes = TabInst->getRefAddr(0);
    69	  if (!RefRes) {
    70	    return false;
    71	  }
    72	  auto Ref = *RefRes;
    73	  EXPECT_TRUE(Ref.isNull());
    74	  EXPECT_TRUE(Ref.getType().isAbsHeapType())
    75	      << "Null reference in concrete-typed table must be normalized to an "
    76	         "abstract heap type (issue #4757)";
    77	  return Ref.isNull() && Ref.getType().isAbsHeapType();
    78	}

   280	/// Regression test for ref.test on externalized nullable references.
   281	///
   282	/// The bug: runRefTestOp always created non-nullable types for externalized
   283	/// references (TypeCode::Ref), discarding the original nullability info.
   284	/// The fix preserves nullability by checking isNullableRefType().
   285	///
   286	/// This test exercises the externalized reference code path in ref.test via
   287	/// the extern.convert_any + ref.test pattern, verifying correct behavior for
   288	/// both nullable and non-nullable ref.test targets, as well as null and
   289	/// non-null input values.

   291	  WasmEdge::Configure Conf;

   293

   298	  // --- Part 1: Non-null anyref input ---
   299	  //
   300	  // When a non-null anyref is externalized via extern.convert_any, the
   301	  // externalized flag is set on the value. The ref.test instruction must
   302	  // correctly handle this externalized type when matching against both
   303	  // nullable and non-nullable extern targets.
   304	  //
   305	  // Note: The runtime parameter-pushing code converts non-null nullable refs
   306	  // to non-nullable before execution. So the externalized type at ref.test
   307	  // time will be non-nullable. Both ref.test targets should succeed.
   308	  {

   312

   314	    std::vector<ValType> ParamTypes = {ValType(TypeCode::AnyRef)};
   315	
   316	    // Test 1: extern.convert_any + ref.test (ref null extern)

   318	    // nullable extern target.
   319	    {
   320	      auto Result = VM.execute("test_nullable", Params, ParamTypes);

   322	      ASSERT_EQ((*Result).size(), 1U);

   324	          << "Non-null externalized anyref should match (ref null extern)";

   326	
   327	    // Test 2: extern.convert_any + ref.test (ref extern)

   329	    // non-nullable extern target (the externalized type is (ref extern)
   330	    // because the runtime made it non-nullable before execution).

2026-05-28 12:27:29,914 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Now let me understand the issue better and look at the `RefVariant` constructor that takes a `ValType`:

When `ValueFromType` is called with a `ValType` like `(ref null $s)` (which has `HTCode = TypeIndex` and `Idx = <index_of_$s>`), it creates `RefVariant(Type)` which calls:

```cpp
RefVariant(const ValType &VT) noexcept { setData<void>(VT); }
```

And `setData` sets the type to the concrete type `(ref null $s)` and the pointer to `nullptr`. This creates a null reference with a concrete type, violating the invariant.

Now, the fix should be in `enterFunction` in `helper.cpp` to normalize the type before pushing. Let me look at how `enterFunction` is structured more completely:

   177	        }
   178	        StackTraceSize =
   179	            compiledStackTrace(StackMgr, InnerStackTrace, StackTrace).size();
   180	        Err = ErrCode(static_cast<ErrCategory>(Code >> 24), Code);
   181	      } else {
   182	        auto &Wrapper = FuncType.getSymbol();
   183	        Wrapper(&ExecutionContext, Func.getSymbol().get(), Args.data(),
   184	                Rets.data());

   186	    } catch (const ErrCode &E) {
   187	      Err = E;

   189	    if (unlikely(Err)) {

   191	        spdlog::error(Err);

   196	              .size();

   198	    }

   200	    // Push returns back to stack.
   201	    for (uint32_t I = 0; I < Rets.size(); ++I) {
   202	      StackMgr.push(Rets[I]);
   203	    }
   204	
   205	    // For compiled function case, the continuation will be the continuation
   206	    // from the popped frame.

   209	    // Native function case: Jump to the start of the function body.
   210

   212	    for (auto &Def : Func.getLocals()) {
   213	      for (uint32_t I = 0; I < Def.first; I++) {
   214	        StackMgr.push(ValueFromType(Def.second));
   215	      }
   216	    }
   217	
   218	    // Push frame.
   219	    // The PC must -1 here because in the interpreter mode execution, the PC
   220	    // will increase after the callee return.

   222	                       RetIt - 1,                  // Return PC

Now let me understand the fix better. The issue is in `enterFunction` at line 214. When we push local variables, we call `ValueFromType(Def.second)` which creates a `RefVariant(Type)` with the raw type. If the type is a concrete type like `(ref null $s)`, the created `RefVariant` has a null pointer but a concrete type.

The fix should normalize the type before creating the `RefVariant`. We should use `toBottomType` to get the abstract bottom type, then create the `RefVariant` with `ValType(TypeCode::RefNull, BotType)`.

But wait, we need `StackMgr` to call `toBottomType`. Let me check if `StackMgr` is available at that point in `enterFunction`:

Looking at the code:
```cpp
for (auto &Def : Func.getLocals()) {
    for (uint32_t I = 0; I < Def.first; I++) {
        StackMgr.push(ValueFromType(Def.second));
    }
}
```

Yes, `StackMgr` is available here. So we can call `toBottomType(StackMgr, Def.second)` to get the bottom type and then create the proper `RefVariant`.

But wait, we need to be careful: for non-reference types, `toBottomType` returns the type code unchanged, which is fine. For reference types, it returns the bottom heap type code. We then use that to construct `ValType(TypeCode::RefNull, BotType)` for the null reference.

   158	    std::vector<ValVariant> Rets(RetsN);
   159	    SavedThreadLocal Saved(*this, StackMgr, Func);
   160	
   161	    ErrCode Err;
   162	    try {
   163	      // Get symbol and execute the function.
   164	      Fault FaultHandler;
   165	      uint32_t Code = PREPARE_FAULT(FaultHandler);
   166	      if (Code != 0) {
   167	        auto InnerStackTrace = FaultHandler.stacktrace();
   168	        {
   169	          std::array<void *, 256> Buffer;
   170	          auto OuterStackTrace = stackTrace(Buffer);
   171	          while (!OuterStackTrace.empty() && !InnerStackTrace.empty() &&
   172	                 InnerStackTrace[InnerStackTrace.size() - 1] ==
   173	                     OuterStackTrace[OuterStackTrace.size() - 1]) {
   174	            InnerStackTrace = InnerStackTrace.first(InnerStackTrace.size() - 1);
   175	            OuterStackTrace = OuterStackTrace.first(OuterStackTrace.size() - 1);
   176	          }
   177	        }
   178	        StackTraceSize =
   179	            compiledStackTrace(StackMgr, InnerStackTrace, StackTrace).size();
   180	        Err = ErrCode(static_cast<ErrCategory>(Code >> 24), Code);
   181	      } else {
   182	        auto &Wrapper = FuncType.getSymbol();
   183	        Wrapper(&ExecutionContext, Func.getSymbol().get(), Args.data(),
   184	                Rets.data());
   185	      }
   186	    } catch (const ErrCode &E) {
   187	      Err = E;
   188	    }
   189	    if (unlikely(Err)) {
   190	      if (Err != ErrCode::Value::Terminated) {
   191	        spdlog::error(Err);
   192	      }
   193	      StackTraceSize +=
   194	          interpreterStackTrace(
   195	              StackMgr, Span<uint32_t>{StackTrace}.subspan(StackTraceSize))
   196	              .size();
   197	      return Unexpect(Err);
   198	    }
   199	
   200	    // Push returns back to stack.
   201	    for (uint32_t I = 0; I < Rets.size(); ++I) {
   202	      StackMgr.push(Rets[I]);
   203	    }
   204	
   205	    // For compiled function case, the continuation will be the continuation
   206	    // from the popped frame.
   207	    return StackMgr.popFrame();
   208	  } else {
   209	    // Native function case: Jump to the start of the function body.
   210

Let me write a small Python script to generate the .wasm binary for the test case

🎬 ACTION
cd /testbed && python3 << 'EOF'
# Generate minimal wasm module for testing the local init bug
# (module
#   (type $s (struct))
#   (func (export "run")
#     (local (ref null $s))
#     local.get 0
#     ref.test (ref null $s)
#     drop
#   )
# )

import struct

def uleb128(v):
    result = []
    while v >= 0x80:
        result.append((v & 0x7f) | 0x80)
        v >>= 7
    result.append(v & 0x7f)
    return bytes(result)

def encode_vector(items):
    return uleb128(len(items)) + b''.join(items)

def encode_section(id, content):
    return bytes([id]) + uleb128(len(content)) + content

# Magic + version
wasm = b'\x00asm\x01\x00\x00\x00'

# Type section (section 1): two types
# type 0: func () -> ()
# type 1: struct $s (no fields)
type_section_content = encode_vector([
    # type 0: func () -> ()
    bytes([0x60, 0, 0]),  # functype: 0 params, 0 results
    # type 1: struct $s
    bytes([0x5f, 0]),     # structtype: 0 fields
])
wasm += encode_section(1, type_section_content)

# Function section (section 3): one function using type 0
wasm += encode_section(3, bytes([1, 0]))  # 1 function, type index 0

# Export section (section 7): export "run" as function 0
name_bytes = b'run'
export = bytes([3]) + uleb128(len(name_bytes)) + name_bytes + bytes([0, 0])  # func export, index 0
wasm += encode_section(7, encode_vector([export]))

# Code section (section 10): one function with locals
# local (ref null $s) = type index 1 with ref null
# The local declaration: count=1, type=(ref null $s)
# ValType encoding for ref null $s: 0x63 0x01 (reftype null, heap type = type index 1)
# But wait, we need to check the encoding:
# ref null $s: 0x63 (ref null) then heap type: if $s is type index 1, heap type is encoded as s33 (signed 33-bit) = 1

# Actually, let me check the encoding more carefully.
# For GC proposal, ref null <heaptype> where heaptype is a type index uses:
# 0x63 (ref null) followed by the type index as a signed 33-bit value in unsigned LEB128
# For type index 1, it's just 0x01

local_type = bytes([0x63, 0x01])  # ref null $s (type index 1)

# Function body:
# local.get 0 = 0x20 0x00
# ref.test (ref null $s) = 0xfb 0x44 0x63 0x01  (ref.test with ref null $s)
# drop = 0x1a
# end = 0x0b

func_body = (
    uleb128(0) +  # 0 local declarations (the param/local is in the function signature)
    uleb128(1) +  # 1 local set
    uleb128(1) +  # 1 local of type
    local_type +   # (ref null $s)
    # instructions:
    bytes([0x20, 0x00]) +  # local.get 0
    bytes([0xfb, 0x44]) +  # ref.test prefix
    local_type +            # ref.test target type: (ref null $s)
    bytes([0x1a]) +         # drop
    bytes([0x0b])           # end
)

wasm += encode_section(10, encode_vector([func_body]))

with open('/tmp/test_local_init.wasm', 'wb') as f:
    f.write(wasm)

print("Wrote /tmp/test_local_init.wasm")
print(f"Size: {len(wasm)} bytes")
print(wasm.hex())
EOF

The export encoding is wrong. Let me fix the Python script:



🎬 ACTION
cd /testbed && python3 << 'EOF'
# Generate minimal wasm module for testing the local init bug
# (module
#   (type $s (struct))
#   (func (export "run")
#     (local (ref null $s))
#     local.get 0
#     ref.test (ref null $s)
#     drop
#   )
# )

import struct

def uleb128(v):
    result = []
    while v >= 0x80:
        result.append((v & 0x7f) | 0x80)
        v >>= 7
    result.append(v & 0x7f)
    return bytes(result)

def encode_vector(items):
    return uleb128(len(items)) + b''.join(items)

def encode_section(id, content):
    return bytes([id]) + uleb128(len(content)) + content

# Magic + version
wasm = b'\x00asm\x01\x00\x00\x00'

# Type section (section 1): two types
# type 0: func () -> ()
# type 1: struct $s (no fields)
type_section_content = encode_vector([
    # type 0: func () -> ()
    bytes([0x60, 0, 0]),  # functype: 0 params, 0 results
    # type 1: struct $s
    bytes([0x5f, 0]),     # structtype: 0 fields
])
wasm += encode_section(1, type_section_content)

# Function section (section 3): one function using type 0
wasm += encode_section(3, bytes([1, 0]))  # 1 function, type index 0

# Export section (section 7): export "run" as function 0
# export: name (len + bytes) + export_kind (0x00 for func) + func_index
name_bytes = b'run'
export = uleb128(len(name_bytes)) + name_bytes + bytes([0x00, 0x00])  # func export, index 0
wasm += encode_section(7, encode_vector([export]))

# Code section (section 10): one function with locals
# local (ref null $s) = type index 1 with ref null
# ValType encoding for ref null $s: 0x63 0x01 (reftype null, heap type = type index 1)
local_type = bytes([0x63, 0x01])  # ref null $s (type index 1)

# Function body:
# local.get 0 = 0x20 0x00
# ref.test (ref null $s) = 0xfb 0x44 0x63 0x01  (ref.test with ref null $s)
# drop = 0x1a
# end = 0x0b

func_body = (
    uleb128(0) +  # 0 local declarations in the compressed form? No...
)

# Wait, I need to understand the code section encoding better.
# In wasm, the code section contains code entries.
# Each code entry: size (uleb128) + code
# Code: local vec + expr
# local vec: count (uleb128) + local entries (each: count (uleb128) + type (ValType))
# expr: instructions + 0x0b (end)

# So for our function with one local of type (ref null $s):
local_entries = uleb128(1) + uleb128(1) + local_type  # 1 set, each with 1 local of given type
expr = bytes([0x20, 0x00]) + bytes([0xfb, 0x44]) + local_type + bytes([0x1a, 0x0b])
code = local_entries + expr
code_entry = uleb128(len(code)) + code

wasm += encode_section(10, encode_vector([code_entry]))

with open('/tmp/test_local_init.wasm', 'wb') as f:
    f.write(wasm)

print("Wrote /tmp/test_local_init.wasm")
print(f"Size: {len(wasm)} bytes")
print(wasm.hex())

Let me fix the Python script:



🎬 ACTION
cd /testbed && python3 << 'EOF'
import struct

def uleb128(v):
    result = []
    while v >= 0x80:
        result.append((v & 0x7f) | 0x80)
        v >>= 7
    result.append(v & 0x7f)
    return bytes(result)

def encode_vector(items):
    return uleb128(len(items)) + b''.join(items)

def encode_section(id, content):
    return bytes([id]) + uleb128(len(content)) + content

# Magic + version
wasm = b'\x00asm\x01\x00\x00\x00'

# Type section (section 1): two types
# type 0: func () -> ()
# type 1: struct $s (no fields)
type_section_content = encode_vector([
    bytes([0x60, 0, 0]),  # functype: 0 params, 0 results
    bytes([0x5f, 0]),     # structtype: 0 fields
])
wasm += encode_section(1, type_section_content)

# Function section (section 3): one function using type 0
wasm += encode_section(3, bytes([1, 0]))

# Export section (section 7): export "run" as function 0
name_bytes = b'run'
export = uleb128(len(name_bytes)) + name_bytes + bytes([0x00, 0x00])
wasm += encode_section(7, encode_vector([export]))

# Code section (section 10)
# local type: ref null $s (type index 1)
local_type = bytes([0x63, 0x01])

# local vec: 1 group, 1 local of type ref null $s
local_entries = uleb128(1) + uleb128(1) + local_type

# instructions: local.get 0, ref.test (ref null $s), drop, end
expr = bytes([0x20, 0x00]) + bytes([0xfb, 0x44]) + local_type + bytes([0x1a, 0x0b])

code = local_entries + expr
code_entry = uleb128(len(code)) + code

wasm += encode_section(10, encode_vector([code_entry]))

with open('/tmp/test_local_init.wasm', 'wb') as f:
    f.write(wasm)

print("Wrote /tmp/test_local_init.wasm")
print(f"Size: {len(wasm)} bytes")
print(wasm.hex())
EOF

I see. Looking at line 153-154:
- `0xfb, 0x15, 0x6d` = `ref.test null eqref` (0x6d = eqref)
- `0xfb, 0x14, 0x00` = `ref.test (ref $s)` with type index 0

So `ref.test null` = `0xFB 0x15` and `ref.test` = `0xFB 0x14`.

For `ref.test (ref null $s)` in the PR, this should be `ref.test null` with heap type `$s` (type index 1), so: `0xFB 0x15 0x01`.

But wait, the PR WAT says `ref.test (ref null $s)`. In the GC proposal, `ref.test` takes a type annotation. If the type is nullable (like `ref null $s`), it uses the `ref.test null` opcode. If non-nullable (like `ref $s`), it uses `ref.test`.

Actually, I need to double-check. Let me look at the existing encoding more carefully. In the NullRefTestWasm at line 153-154:
```
0xfb, 0x15, 0x6d, ...  -> ref.test null eqref
0xfb, 0x14, 0x00, ...  -> ref.test (ref $s)   (type index 0)
```

So for the PR example: `ref.test (ref null $s)` where `$s` is type index 1, this should be `0xFB 0x15 0x01`.

Let me fix the Python script:







🎬 ACTION
cd /testbed && python3 << 'EOF'
import struct

def uleb128(v):
    result = []
    while v >= 0x80:
        result.append((v & 0x7f) | 0x80)
        v >>= 7
    result.append(v & 0x7f)
    return bytes(result)

def encode_vector(items):
    return uleb128(len(items)) + b''.join(items)

def encode_section(id, content):
    return bytes([id]) + uleb128(len(content)) + content

# Magic + version
wasm = b'\x00asm\x01\x00\x00\x00'

# Type section (section 1): two types
# type 0: func () -> ()
# type 1: struct $s (no fields)
type_section_content = encode_vector([
    bytes([0x60, 0, 0]),  # functype: 0 params, 0 results
    bytes([0x5f, 0]),     # structtype: 0 fields
])
wasm += encode_section(1, type_section_content)

# Function section (section 3): one function using type 0
wasm += encode_section(3, bytes([1, 0]))

# Export section (section 7): export "run" as function 0
name_bytes = b'run'
export = uleb128(len(name_bytes)) + name_bytes + bytes([0x00, 0x00])
wasm += encode_section(7, encode_vector([export]))

# Code section (section 10)
# local type: ref null $s (type index 1)
# 0x63 = ref null, 0x01 = type index 1
local_type = bytes([0x63, 0x01])

# local vec: 1 group, 1 local of type ref null $s
local_entries = uleb128(1) + uleb128(1) + local_type

# instructions: local.get 0, ref.test null $s, drop, end
# ref.test null: 0xFB 0x15, then heap type $s = type index 1
expr = bytes([0x20, 0x00]) + bytes([0xfb, 0x15]) + bytes([0x01]) + bytes([0x1a, 0x0b])

code = local_entries + expr
code_entry = uleb128(len(code)) + code

wasm += encode_section(10, encode_vector([code_entry]))

with open('/tmp/test_local_init.wasm', 'wb') as f:
    f.write(wasm)

print("Wrote /tmp/test_local_init.wasm")
print(f"Size: {len(wasm)} bytes")
print(wasm.hex())
EOF

```cpp
TypeCode Executor::toBottomType(Runtime::StackManager &StackMgr,
                                const ValType &Type) const {
  if (Type.isRefType()) {
    if (Type.isAbsHeapType()) {
      // ... returns bottom abstract type
    } else {
      const auto &CompType =
          (*StackMgr.getModule()->getType(Type.getTypeIndex()))
              ->getCompositeType();
      // ...
    }
  }
}
```

     9	///
    10	/// \file
    11	/// This file contains the base class definition of composite instances
    12	/// (function, struct, and array).
    13	///
    14	//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//
    15	#pragma once
    16	
    17	#include "ast/type.h"
    18	#include "common/types.h"
    19	
    20	#include <vector>
    21	
    22	namespace WasmEdge {
    23	namespace Runtime {
    24	namespace Instance {
    25	
    26	class ModuleInstance;
    27	
    28	class CompositeBase {
    29	public:
    30	  /// Constructor for only host function instance case.
    31	  CompositeBase() noexcept : ModInst(nullptr), TypeIdx(0) {}
    32	  /// Constructor for function, array, and struct instances.
    33	  CompositeBase(const ModuleInstance *Mod, const uint32_t Idx) noexcept
    34	      : ModInst(Mod), TypeIdx(Idx) {
    35	    assuming(ModInst);
    36	  }
    37	
    38	  /// Getter of module instance of this instance.
    39	  const ModuleInstance *getModule() const noexcept { return ModInst; }
    40	
    41	  /// Getter of closed type index of this instance in the module.
    42	  uint32_t getTypeIndex() const noexcept { return TypeIdx; }
    43	
    44	  /// Getter of value type in defined type form.
    45	  ValType getDefType() const noexcept {
    46	    if (ModInst) {
    47	      return ValType(TypeCode::Ref, TypeIdx);
    48	    } else {
    49	      // nullptr `ModInst` case is only for host function instance case.
    50	      return ValType(TypeCode::Ref, TypeCode::FuncRef);
    51	    }
    52	  }
    53	
    54	protected:
    55	  friend class ModuleInstance;
    56	  void linkDefinedType(const ModuleInstance *Mod,
    57	                       const uint32_t Index) noexcept {
    58	    assuming(Mod);
    59	    ModInst = Mod;
    60	    TypeIdx = Index;
    61	  }
    62	
    63	  /// \name Data of composite instances.
    64	  /// @{
    65	  const ModuleInstance *ModInst;
    66	  uint32_t TypeIdx;
    67	  /// @}
    68	};

Good. So `Func.getModule()` gives us the module instance. But the issue is that `toBottomType` uses `StackMgr.getModule()` which returns `nullptr` because no frame has been pushed yet.

1. Use `Func.getModule()` to get the module instance for the `toBottomType` call

Actually, let me think about this more carefully. The `toBottomType` function does:
- If the type is an abstract heap type, return the corresponding null variant
- If the type has a type index (concrete type), look up the type from the module and determine if it's a function type or a struct/array type, then return the appropriate bottom null type

But for the local initialization, we know the type is always nullable (locals are always declared with `ref null`), and the value is always null. The question is: what abstract type should we use?

For a concrete type like `(ref null $s)` where `$s` is a struct, the bottom type should be `NullRef` (which represents "none" - the bottom of the type hierarchy for struct/array types). For a function reference, it should be `NullFuncRef`. For an extern reference, `NullExternRef`.

But wait, I can simplify this. Looking at `toBottomType`, when it has a type index (non-abstract), it checks the composite type:
- If it's a function type → `NullFuncRef`
- Otherwise (struct/array) → `NullRef`

This is exactly what we need. But we need a valid module instance to call `toBottomType`. 

Instead of calling `toBottomType` which uses `StackMgr.getModule()`, I can inline the logic using `Func.getModule()`. But a better approach might be to simply move the frame push before the local push, so `StackMgr.getModule()` is available. Let me check if that's feasible.

   104	  void pushFrame(const Instance::ModuleInstance *Module,
   105	                 AST::InstrView::iterator From, uint32_t LocalNum = 0,
   106	                 uint32_t Arity = 0, bool IsTailCall = false) noexcept {
   107	    if (!IsTailCall) {
   108	      FrameStack.emplace_back(Module, From, LocalNum, Arity,
   109	                              static_cast<uint32_t>(ValueStack.size()));
   110	    } else {
   111	      assuming(!FrameStack.empty());
   112	      assuming(FrameStack.back().VPos >= FrameStack.back().Locals);
   113	      assuming(FrameStack.back().VPos - FrameStack.back().Locals <=
   114	               ValueStack.size() - LocalNum);
   115	      ValueStack.erase(ValueStack.begin() + FrameStack.back().VPos -
   116	                           FrameStack.back().Locals,
   117	                       ValueStack.end() - LocalNum);
   118	      FrameStack.back().Module = Module;
   119	      FrameStack.back().Locals = LocalNum;
   120	      FrameStack.back().Arity = Arity;
   121	      FrameStack.back().VPos = static_cast<uint32_t>(ValueStack.size());
   122	      FrameStack.back().HandlerStack.clear();
   123	    }
   124	  }
   125	
   126	  /// Unsafe pop top frame.
   127	  AST::InstrView::iterator popFrame() noexcept {
   128	    assuming(!FrameStack.empty());
   129	    assuming(FrameStack.back().VPos >= FrameStack.back().Locals);
   130	    assuming(FrameStack.back().VPos - FrameStack.back().Locals <=
   131	             ValueStack.size() - FrameStack.back().Arity);
   132	    ValueStack.erase(ValueStack.begin() + FrameStack.back().VPos -
   133	                         FrameStack.back().Locals,
   134	                     ValueStack.end() - FrameStack.back().Arity);
   135	    auto From = FrameStack.back().From;
   136	    FrameStack.pop_back();
   137	    return From;

Looking at the table constructor in `table.h` line 33-35:
```cpp
TableInstance(const AST::TableType &TType) noexcept
    : TabType(TType),
      Refs(TType.getLimit().getMin(), RefVariant(TType.getRefType())),
```

This is called from the C API (`WasmEdge_TableInstanceCreate`) and from `table.cpp` line 31 (when there IS an init expression). The case without an init expression goes through `table.cpp` line 37 which already normalizes. But the `TableInstance` constructor is still called directly with potentially concrete types from:
1. `table.cpp` line 31: `ModInst.addTable(TabSeg.getTableType(), InitTabValue)` - this uses the second constructor with `InitVal`, not the first one.
2. C API `WasmEdge_TableInstanceCreate` - uses the first constructor with just `TType`.

But wait, the first constructor at line 33-38 fills the table with `RefVariant(TType.getRefType())` which could have a concrete type. However, this constructor also has `assuming(TType.getRefType().isNullableRefType())` which means it's only used for nullable types. And the table entries initialized this way would have concrete types, which could cause the same crash.

But that's a separate issue from this PR. The PR specifically is about function-local initialization.

Now let me also think about whether my fix handles all cases correctly. Let me look at the full `enterFunction` to check if there's another path that pushes locals:

Let me also test the `ref.cast` variant:







🎬 ACTION
cd /testbed && python3 << 'EOF'
import struct

def uleb128(v):
    result = []
    while v >= 0x80:
        result.append((v & 0x7f) | 0x80)
        v >>= 7
    result.append(v & 0x7f)
    return bytes(result)

def encode_vector(items):
    return uleb128(len(items)) + b''.join(items)

def encode_section(id, content):
    return bytes([id]) + uleb128(len(content)) + content

# Test 1: ref.cast on default-initialized local with concrete ref type
# (module
#   (type $s (struct))
#   (func (export "run")
#     (local (ref null $s))
#     local.get 0
#     ref.cast null $s
#     drop
#   )
# )

wasm = b'\x00asm\x01\x00\x00\x00'
type_section_content = encode_vector([
    bytes([0x60, 0, 0]),  # functype: () -> ()
    bytes([0x5f, 0]),     # structtype: $s
])
wasm += encode_section(1, type_section_content)
wasm += encode_section(3, bytes([1, 0]))
name_bytes = b'run'
export = uleb128(len(name_bytes)) + name_bytes + bytes([0x00, 0x00])
wasm += encode_section(7, encode_vector([export]))

local_type = bytes([0x63, 0x01])  # ref null $s
local_entries = uleb128(1) + uleb128(1) + local_type
# ref.cast null $s: 0xFB 0x17 (ref.cast null), then heap type $s = type index 1
expr = bytes([0x20, 0x00]) + bytes([0xfb, 0x17]) + bytes([0x01]) + bytes([0x1a, 0x0b])
code = local_entries + expr
code_entry = uleb128(len(code)) + code
wasm += encode_section(10, encode_vector([code_entry]))

with open('/tmp/test_local_cast.wasm', 'wb') as f:
    f.write(wasm)
print("Wrote test_local_cast.wasm")
print(wasm.hex())
EOF

Now I'm fairly confident the fix is correct. But let me also think about whether there's a simpler/cleaner fix. Instead of duplicating the logic from `toBottomType`, I could modify the code to push the frame first, then use `toBottomType` with the stack manager. But that would require changing the frame push order which might have other implications.

Alternatively, I could modify `ValueFromType` to accept an optional module pointer to do the normalization. But that would change the API.

The current approach is fine. Let me also check if there's any issue with the `exnref` type (exception references). Looking at `toBottomType`:

```cpp
case TypeCode::NullExnRef:
case TypeCode::ExnRef:
    return TypeCode::NullExnRef;
```

But for concrete types that are exception types, it would go to the else branch and return `NullRef`. Is that correct? Let me check: if we have a concrete exception type, the composite type would be... Actually, exception types are not composite types (struct/array/func). Let me check what types can appear as concrete heap types.

Looking at the GC proposal, concrete heap types are:
- Function types (type index pointing to a `functype`)
- Struct types (type index pointing to a `structtype`)
- Array types (type index pointing to an `arraytype`)

The `toBottomType` function checks `CompType.isFunc()` and returns `NullFuncRef` if it's a function, otherwise returns `NullRef`. This is correct because the only other options are struct and array types.

But wait, there might also be exception types in the future. However, for now the code handles it correctly.

Let me also double-check: is there any case where `Func.getModule()` could be nullptr in the native function path? Looking at the `FunctionInstance` constructors, for native wasm functions, `ModInst` is always set (the constructors have `assuming(ModInst)`). And the native function path (`Func.isWasmFunction()`) should always have a module. So this is safe.

Now let me look at one more thing: the `RefVariant` constructor that takes a `ValType` alone. Could there be other places that call `RefVariant(Type)` with a concrete type? Let me check the table constructor again:

Looking at `table.h` line 33-36:
```cpp
TableInstance(const AST::TableType &TType) noexcept
    : TabType(TType),
      Refs(TType.getLimit().getMin(), RefVariant(TType.getRefType())),
      InitValue(RefVariant(TType.getRefType())) {
```

This creates `RefVariant(TType.getRefType())` where `TType.getRefType()` could be a concrete type. However, this constructor is only called from:
1. `WasmEdge_TableInstanceCreate` in the C API
2. The table instantiation path when there IS an init expression (which then fills with proper values)

For case 1, the C API creates a table with default null values. If the table has a concrete type like `(ref null $s)`, the null references will have concrete types, which could cause the same crash. But this is a separate issue from the PR (the PR is about function locals).

However, I should note that my fix only addresses the function-local initialization path. The table initialization path was already partially fixed in PR #4764 (for the case without an init expression). The case with an init expression and the C API case might still be vulnerable, but those are separate issues.

cd /testbed && python3 << 'EOF'
import struct

def uleb128(v):
    result = []
    while v >= 0x80:
        result.append((v & 0x7f) | 0x80)
        v >>= 7
    result.append(v & 0x7f)
    return bytes(result)

def encode_vector(items):
    return uleb128(len(items)) + b''.join(items)

def encode_section(id, content):
    return bytes([id]) + uleb128(len(content)) + content

# Test: table with concrete type, no init expression (the case that was fixed)
# (module
#   (type $s (struct))
#   (table $t (export "t") 1 (ref null $s))
#   (func (export "run")
#     i32.const 0
#     table.get $t
#     ref.test null $s
#     drop
#   )
# )

wasm = b'\x00asm\x01\x00\x00\x00'
type_section_content = encode_vector([
    bytes([0x60, 0, 0]),  # functype: () -> ()
    bytes([0x5f, 0]),     # structtype: $s
])
wasm += encode_section(1, type_section_content)
wasm += encode_section(3, bytes([1, 0]))

# Table section: 1 table, ref null $s, limits: min=1, max=1
table_type = bytes([0x63, 0x01, 0x01, 0x01])  # ref null $s, min=1, max=1
wasm += encode_section(4, encode_vector([table_type]))

# Export "t" as table 0
name_bytes = b't'
export_t = uleb128(len(name_bytes)) + name_bytes + bytes([0x01, 0x00])  # table export
# Export "run" as func 0
name_bytes2 = b'run'
export_run = uleb128(len(name_bytes2)) + name_bytes2 + bytes([0x00, 0x00])  # func export
wasm += encode_section(7, encode_vector([export_t, export_run]))

# Code section
local_entries = uleb128(0)  # no locals
# i32.const 0, table.get 0, ref.test null $s, drop, end
expr = bytes([0x41, 0x00]) + bytes([0x25, 0x00]) + bytes([0xfb, 0x15, 0x01]) + bytes([0x1a, 0x0b])
code = local_entries + expr
code_entry = uleb128(len(code)) + code
wasm += encode_section(10, encode_vector([code_entry]))

with open('/tmp/test_table_ref.wasm', 'wb') as f:
    f.write(wasm)
print("Wrote test_table_ref.wasm")
print(wasm.hex())
EOF

import struct

def uleb128(v):
    result = []
    while v >= 0x80:
        result.append((v & 0x7f) | 0x80)
        v >>= 7
    result.append(v & 0x7f)
    return bytes(result)

def encode_vector(items):
    return uleb128(len(items)) + b''.join(items)

def encode_section(id, content):
    return bytes([id]) + uleb128(len(content)) + content

# Test: table with concrete type, no init expression (the case that was fixed)
# (module
#   (type $s (struct))
#   (table $t (export "t") 1 (ref null $s))
#   (func (export "run")
#     i32.const 0
#     table.get $t
#     ref.test null $s
#     drop
#   )
# )

wasm = b'\x00asm\x01\x00\x00\x00'
type_section_content = encode_vector([
    bytes([0x60, 0, 0]),  # functype: () -> ()
    bytes([0x5f, 0]),     # structtype: $s
])
wasm += encode_section(1, type_section_content)
wasm += encode_section(3, bytes([1, 0]))

# Table section: 1 table
# Each table: reftype + limits
# ref null $s = 0x63 0x01
# limits: 0x01 (with max) + min=1 + max=1
table_entry = bytes([0x63, 0x01, 0x01, 0x01, 0x01])  # ref null $s, flags=1 (has max), min=1, max=1
wasm += encode_section(4, encode_vector([table_entry]))

# Export "t" as table 0
name_bytes = b't'
export_t = uleb128(len(name_bytes)) + name_bytes + bytes([0x01, 0x00])  # table export
# Export "run" as func 0
name_bytes2 = b'run'
export_run = uleb128(len(name_bytes2)) + name_bytes2 + bytes([0x00, 0x00])  # func export
wasm += encode_section(7, encode_vector([export_t, export_run]))

# Code section
local_entries = uleb128(0)  # no locals
# i32.const 0, table.get 0, ref.test null $s, drop, end
expr = bytes([0x41, 0x00]) + bytes([0x25, 0x00]) + bytes([0xfb, 0x15, 0x01]) + bytes([0x1a, 0x0b])
code = local_entries + expr
code_entry = uleb128(len(code)) + code
wasm += encode_section(10, encode_vector([code_entry]))

with open('/tmp/test_table_ref.wasm', 'wb') as f:
    f.write(wasm)
print("Wrote test_table_ref.wasm")
print(wasm.hex())

This is the `br_on_cast` handler. It has the same issue: if `VT` is not an abstract heap type (i.e., concrete type), it dereferences `Val.getPtr<Runtime::Instance::CompositeBase>()` which could be null. But the comments say "Reference must not be nullptr here because the null references are typed with the least abstract heap type." So this code assumes the invariant that null references always have abstract heap types. My fix ensures that invariant holds for function locals, so this code should be safe now.

Similarly, `proxy.cpp` lines 369 and 397 have the same pattern.

Now I'm confident my fix is correct. Let me also check if there's any issue with the `externref` type. Looking at my condition:

```cpp
if (Def.second.isRefType() && !Def.second.isAbsHeapType()) {
```

For `externref`, `isAbsHeapType()` returns true (since `HTCode` is `ExternRef` or `NullExternRef`), so we go to the else branch which calls `ValueFromType`. That creates `RefVariant(Type)` where `Type` is e.g. `(ref null extern)`. This is correct because `externref` is already an abstract type.

For `anyref`, `eqref`, `i31ref`, `structref`, `arrayref`, `funcref` - same, they're all abstract.

For concrete types like `(ref null $s)` where `$s` is a struct type, `isAbsHeapType()` is false, so we normalize to `NullRef`.

For concrete types like `(ref null $f)` where `$f` is a function type, `isAbsHeapType()` is false, so we normalize to `NullFuncRef`.

This matches exactly what `toBottomType` does.

I believe the fix is complete and correct. Let me also make sure the build works for all targets

The fix looks good. Let me also think about potential improvements:

1. The condition `Def.second.isRefType() && !Def.second.isAbsHeapType()` correctly identifies concrete reference types that need normalization.

2. For the abstract case (when `isAbsHeapType()` returns true), we fall through to `ValueFromType` which creates `RefVariant(Type)`. This is correct because abstract types already satisfy the invariant.

3. The normalization logic correctly distinguishes between function types (`NullFuncRef`) and struct/array types (`NullRef`), matching the behavior of `toBottomType`.

4. We use `Func.getModule()` which is guaranteed to be non-null for native wasm functions.

This fix mirrors the approach used for tables in `table.cpp` (PR #4764), but adapted for the function-local initialization path where the stack frame hasn't been pushed yet.

Let me submit.
